  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7c1b0be1-26e4-453f-a418-a27fdbe55cb6'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer3336863988977581095">A rare meteorite struck Alex Woods when he was ten years old, leaving scars and marking him for an extraordinary future. The son of a fortune teller, bookish, and an easy target for bullies, Alex hasn't had the easiest childhood.<br/><br/>But when he meets curmudgeonly widower Mr. Peterson, he finds an unlikely friend. Someone who teaches him that you only get one shot at life. That</span>
  <span id="freeText3336863988977581095" style="display:none">A rare meteorite struck Alex Woods when he was ten years old, leaving scars and marking him for an extraordinary future. The son of a fortune teller, bookish, and an easy target for bullies, Alex hasn't had the easiest childhood.<br /><br />But when he meets curmudgeonly widower Mr. Peterson, he finds an unlikely friend. Someone who teaches him that you only get one shot at life. That you have to make it count.<br /><br />So when, aged seventeen, Alex is stopped at customs with 113 grams of marijuana, an urn full of ashes on the front seat, and an entire nation in uproar, he's fairly sure he's done the right thing ...<br /><br />Introducing a bright young voice destined to charm the world,<i> The Universe Versus Alex Woods</i> is a celebration of curious incidents, astronomy and astrology, the works of Kurt Vonnegut and the unexpected connections that form our world.</span>

<div id="review_660451674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660451674" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/154540-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1185836523p2/154540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/660451674?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/154540-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660451674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2030718330058419287">Sometimes, life just lines up in a way that seems like it isn't just a coincidence. Like this:<br/><br/>I'm teaching Vonnegut's <i>Slaughterhouse-Five</i> this fall, so I re-read the book last week. Then, Gaiman's new book was released, and I read that one. I signed into Goodreads to review <i>The Ocean at the End of the Lane</i> (which was really good) and saw Gaiman's recommendation for <i>The Universe Versus Alex Woods</i>. I bought the book without reading more about it because I needed something to read on vacation, and </span>
  <span id="freeText2030718330058419287" style="display:none">Sometimes, life just lines up in a way that seems like it isn't just a coincidence. Like this:<br /><br />I'm teaching Vonnegut's <i>Slaughterhouse-Five</i> this fall, so I re-read the book last week. Then, Gaiman's new book was released, and I read that one. I signed into Goodreads to review <i>The Ocean at the End of the Lane</i> (which was really good) and saw Gaiman's recommendation for <i>The Universe Versus Alex Woods</i>. I bought the book without reading more about it because I needed something to read on vacation, and I liked the cover.<br /><br />And, if you're reading this review, then you probably already know what I didn't know -- that this book centers around Vonnegut, and devotes a significant part of the book to <i>Slaughterhouse-Five</i>. <br /><br />What Extence gets absolutely right in this book is the mixture of naivety with sincerity with a clear sense of irony. It doesn't have the level of absurdity of Vonnegut but that's not the point of this book, so don't expect any Tralfamadorians.<br /><br />In another perfect moment, while I was thinking about this book, I listed to a song that has a lyric from a Sydney Lanier poem: "music is love in search of a word." This book and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the moment when Alex and Mr. Peterson listened to music as he died instead of talking and  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> this thought all go together: this book is love all captured in words.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_645747690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645747690" />
    <a title="Erin Laidley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18746274-erin-laidley"><img alt="Erin Laidley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570398307p2/18746274.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645747690?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin Laidley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin Laidley" href="/user/show/18746274-erin-laidley">Erin Laidley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18746274-erin-laidley?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645747690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11106666118252102215">The best description that I can think of for this book is that it reminded me of "a mixture of <i>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</i>, <i>Up</i>, <i>The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time</i>, and <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>." While that may seem like a strange combination, elements from all of these works are seamlessly combined to create a humorous, poignant novel that will leave a lasting impression.<br/><br/><i>The Universe Versus Alex Woods</i> is written as a first person retrospective narrative in the style of Kurt</span>
  <span id="freeText11106666118252102215" style="display:none">The best description that I can think of for this book is that it reminded me of "a mixture of <i>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</i>, <i>Up</i>, <i>The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time</i>, and <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>." While that may seem like a strange combination, elements from all of these works are seamlessly combined to create a humorous, poignant novel that will leave a lasting impression.<br /><br /><i>The Universe Versus Alex Woods</i> is written as a first person retrospective narrative in the style of Kurt Vonnegut, whose works play a rather important role in the novel: the reader is immediately exposed to the action at the end of Alex's story, and is then brought back to the beginning to see how the events leading up to the present situation influenced and shaped his personality and worldview. At first glance, it is a coming of age story about a young boy, Alex, who lives a very unconventional life: he doesn't know who his father is, his mother reads Tarot cards, he is a bit of a celebrity after having been struck by a meteorite when he was young, and his best friend is a Vietnam veteran. However, it is also a thought-provoking work of fiction that deals with many heavy subjects - such as bullying, free will, life, death, euthanasia and morality - in a respectful and meaningful way.<br /><br />The protagonist, Alex, is a logical, naive, introverted young man with a compelling, authentic voice. There is a lot of social disconnect between him and his peers, due to the fact that he enjoys learning, voices his opinions - regardless of their appropriateness - and tends to go off on many tangents. As a biology student, I found all of the detailed information that Alex provided in regards to his scientific learning to be very interesting (which, from what I've seen, places me in the minority on that count). It is hard not to empathize with Alex, whose childlike innocence and unique worldview make him quite easy to like.<br /><br />The friendship between Alex and Mr. Peterson is very much like that of Russell and Carl in <i>Up</i>: a young boy befriends a grouchy old man who lost his wife, and eventually the two begin to consider each other as a family of sorts. I loved watching this friendship grow and develop. Though it was filled with difficulties, the influence that this friendship had on both parties was quite powerful - especially towards the end where it is shown just how much they are willing to do for each other. At the beginning of the novel, Alex is a boy, but with Mr. Peterson's help, he becomes a man with a heightened sense of integrity and a new outlook on life.<br /><br />Overall, this was an excellent novel that will leave you with many ethical and existential questions, and will inspire you to read some of Kurt Vonnegut's works.<br /><br /><i> This review can also be found at <a href="http://theinbetweenplace.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The In-Between Place</a>. Thanks to Netgalley for providing me with an advanced copy of this work in exchange for an honest review. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11106666118252102215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Yodamom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905141-yodamom"><img alt="Yodamom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526248248p2/2905141.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905141-yodamom?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905141-yodamom?shelf=trauma-recovery">trauma-recovery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905141-yodamom?shelf=new-authors">new-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905141-yodamom?shelf=tissue-box-special">tissue-box-special</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer640779926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15466057659920801948"><br/>It all started with a drive, thirteen grams of marijuana and an urn of ashes. This is the story of Alex Woods from the age of 10 to 17. Alex is one unique and complex character. His life was shattered into a new realm when at age 10 a meteor crashed through his bathroom ceiling and hit him on the head. He lives with his mother a tarot card reader and is receptive to more than most. She doesn't try to fit in and her beliefs are not mainstream. He is already seen as different in his community. Aft</span>
  <span id="freeText15466057659920801948" style="display:none"><br>It all started with a drive, thirteen grams of marijuana and an urn of ashes. This is the story of Alex Woods from the age of 10 to 17. Alex is one unique and complex character. His life was shattered into a new realm when at age 10 a meteor crashed through his bathroom ceiling and hit him on the head. He lives with his mother a tarot card reader and is receptive to more than most. She doesn't try to fit in and her beliefs are not mainstream. He is already seen as different in his community. After his accident, he becomes almost famous, stalked by paparazzi and reporters. He is also stalked by the school's bullies. These bullies are truly rotten, mean and nasty. Even with all that they lead him down a path of wonderful discoveries and friendship they direct him on a path of great discovery. His tale of the next 7 years is a wonderland of growing up and being different, of learning self control and who he really is and where he wants to fit into the world.The first chapter had me sitting on the edge of my seat with a level of excitement one has when you can feel a great book beginning and it carried to the end. I just wanted to sit in the shade, drink my tea and slip into the life of Alex. It is not a book that should be rushed, but taken slowly, savored. Every emotion is touched and some hit hard where it hurts. A lovely story.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425297ra/848678.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15466057659920801948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_619498965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619498965" />
    <a title="Fiona Robson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5898097-fiona-robson"><img alt="Fiona Robson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361050509p2/5898097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619498965?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona Robson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona Robson" href="/user/show/5898097-fiona-robson">Fiona Robson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3516350466411781990">“A tale of an unexpected friendship, an unlikely hero and an improbable journey...This novel might just strike you as one of the funniest, most heartbreaking novels you've ever read. This is the story of seventeen-year-old Alex Woods - born to a clairvoyant mother and a phantom father, victim of an improbable childhood accident - who is stopped at Dover customs in possession of 113 grams of marijuana and the ashes of his best friend, Vietnam veteran Isaac Peterson. What follows is a highly origi</span>
  <span id="freeText3516350466411781990" style="display:none">“A tale of an unexpected friendship, an unlikely hero and an improbable journey...This novel might just strike you as one of the funniest, most heartbreaking novels you've ever read. This is the story of seventeen-year-old Alex Woods - born to a clairvoyant mother and a phantom father, victim of an improbable childhood accident - who is stopped at Dover customs in possession of 113 grams of marijuana and the ashes of his best friend, Vietnam veteran Isaac Peterson. What follows is a highly original and compelling account of Alex's life and the strange series of events that brought him here.”<br /><br />Actually … ignore the above. This story was not funny or heartwarming in the slightest and I hated it! There was absolutely nothing profound and witty in the whole thing. I think the only thing which attracted me to it at all was that it had a lovely pic of Glastonbury Tor on the front, and iBooks had given it a good review. The characters largely annoyed me, especially the hippy dippy mother. Was glad to get this one done and over with!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_818561168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/818561168" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/818561168?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer818561168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7642170728449962950">Oh, wow. The Universe Versus Alex Woods starts off seeming like it's gonna be a quirky sort of book: the narration is matter of fact where it possibly shouldn't be, and the situation Alex is in on the opening pages is an interesting one. Unfortunately for everyone who picked it up on the basis of that, it's not really the kind of book it turned out to be. I don't know that I'd call it funny -- it's not laugh out loud funny, anyway; more "wry smiles" funny -- and I don't know that I'd call it hea</span>
  <span id="freeText7642170728449962950" style="display:none">Oh, wow. The Universe Versus Alex Woods starts off seeming like it's gonna be a quirky sort of book: the narration is matter of fact where it possibly shouldn't be, and the situation Alex is in on the opening pages is an interesting one. Unfortunately for everyone who picked it up on the basis of that, it's not really the kind of book it turned out to be. I don't know that I'd call it funny -- it's not laugh out loud funny, anyway; more "wry smiles" funny -- and I don't know that I'd call it heartbreaking, either. It made me cry, but the simplicity of the narrative voice kept it from being maudlin, from dwelling too much on any of the important details, which is what for me made them strike all the more forcefully.<br /><br />It <i>is</i> the story of an unlikely friendship, that's definitely true, and it's a beautiful story from my point of view. It's fairly apparent from the first chapter, to me, what exactly is going on here: what matters is how we get there, and how much less funny/quirky it seems by the end, and how much more sad and true and beautiful. But if you don't want to know, don't read any further in this review.<br /><br />What was apparent to me from the beginning is that this is a book about an assisted suicide. It didn't even need to be stated clearly: trying to get back into the country at Dover, the urn of ashes, somehow it all just clicked for me. Possibly because this is an issue that I've thought about at great length, forwards and backwards. Because if I were Alex Woods, I'd do exactly the same things, in exactly that order, and I would feel exactly as right about it. <br /><br />The friendship between the two is the fun and quirky part; the fact that, when Mr. Peterson becomes ill, Alex chooses to take care of him, and then to make sure that he is also allowed to die when he's ready, and the understanding between the two... This is an idealised version of how this might happen, and the fact that Alex narrates means that we don't pull up and see this from another character's point of view -- how they might worry about Alex's reactions, how he might feel -- and that might make some people feel that this is a book somehow advocating for euthanasia. Which I think it is, but only in the sense that it makes it clear that to be allowed a choice about how and when we die makes it a lot easier <i>to die</i> -- and that for some people 'how' and 'when' might be very clearly defined, as they are for Mr. Peterson. But I don't think it advocates euthanasia as the <i>only</i> way. It just emphasises <i>choice</i>, and how very comforting it is to many people to know that they have control over even that last inevitability. It even emphasises choice in smaller matters, like what drugs you take.<br /><br />If you don't understand why someone would want assisted suicide, this might help. If you don't understand why someone would want to help someone commit suicide, I think this would definitely help. And if you already understand both of those things, then it's still something that articulates all this very clearly, and might just give you words or clarity for yourself in the future.<br /><br />I am definitely, definitely keeping this book. I will probably lend it to people, and I hope I never need to read it again myself, but I can imagine times when I might want to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7642170728449962950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441708311" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4103984435265348124">The tale of Alex Woods, age 17, as told by himself, in a steady, logical, borderline-autistic voice. <br/><br/>Struck on the head by a meteorite when he was a child, Alex lives a quietly extraordinary life. An epileptic, obsessed by maths and astronomy, Alex is a deeply geeky, lonely boy with few friends but a complex inner life. The story is rich in references - His Dark Materials, A Prayer for Owen Meany, One Flew Over the Cuckoos Nest, Catch 22, Schubert - but most of all, Kurt Vonnegut, who Alex disco</span>
  <span id="freeText4103984435265348124" style="display:none">The tale of Alex Woods, age 17, as told by himself, in a steady, logical, borderline-autistic voice. <br /><br />Struck on the head by a meteorite when he was a child, Alex lives a quietly extraordinary life. An epileptic, obsessed by maths and astronomy, Alex is a deeply geeky, lonely boy with few friends but a complex inner life. The story is rich in references - His Dark Materials, A Prayer for Owen Meany, One Flew Over the Cuckoos Nest, Catch 22, Schubert - but most of all, Kurt Vonnegut, who Alex discovers through his accidental friendship with a Vietnam vet, a friendship destined to change the entire course of Alex’s life. <br /><br />This is, in many ways, a very profound book, that philosophises on the meaning of life and death - or lack of meaning; Alex is something of an existentialist. Which is not to say Alex Woods Versus the Universe is in any way dry or dull or even worthy; it’s a consistently entertaining and very funny – laugh out loud funny – read, which I highly recommend.</span>

<div id="review_652035034" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/652035034" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18349293-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397357262p2/18349293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/652035034?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/18349293-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18040322-the-universe-versus-alex-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18349293-melissa?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer652035034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7674744903835831779">What a sweet book. It's about a boy from a small town in England who is odd and a loner, but also very smart and likeable. He rather reminds me of the autistic kid in Memoirs of an Imaginary Friend - or the main character of The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night Time - but more social and less autistic - but he seems like he's on the spectrum or at least a kid with some quirks. Toward the middle of the book, I start seeing similarities to John Green's The Fault in Our Stars. BTW, if you h</span>
  <span id="freeText7674744903835831779" style="display:none">What a sweet book. It's about a boy from a small town in England who is odd and a loner, but also very smart and likeable. He rather reminds me of the autistic kid in Memoirs of an Imaginary Friend - or the main character of The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night Time - but more social and less autistic - but he seems like he's on the spectrum or at least a kid with some quirks. Toward the middle of the book, I start seeing similarities to John Green's The Fault in Our Stars. BTW, if you have not read any of the three books I just mentioned, add them to your pile as they are 4-5 star books.<br /><br />It's also about a gruff solitary old man, also smart and sweet on the inside - and how they meet and their relationship as it evolves and what it means to the both of them. Other characters who make an appearance are the boy's mother, a beloved dog, an older sister type figure (friend) from school and other minor characters such as kids at school, some bullies, some not, neighbors, etc.<br /><br />It is written in an odd way, it starts at the end, goes to the beginning and skips around a bit, but by about 1/4 way through, you are hooked and everything makes sense, things start clicking into place like magnets and you are rolling down the reader track eagerly anticipating every event as it unfolds. At it's most basic, it sounds like a typical boy/man bonding story that's been done a hundred times, but it has surprising twists and a modern slant. This would have been 4 star except I kicked it up to 5 because sometimes 5 star books for me are where I learned new things, I learned a ton about Kurt Vonnegut, astrophysics, growing marijuana and epilepsy. What an odd combination, right? Well, it isn't fair to leak out too much more of the story, you'll have to read it yourself to see how it all fits together. I recommend everyone read this book.<br /><br />I must add: for those of you with sensitive eyes and constitutions, I must say there are bad words, both British and American. If you have read the description, there is also marijuana use and cultivation, that is very casual and matter of fact, although the main character (young teen) does caution the other person not to use marijuana because it's not good for him - so there is that. Anyway, if these things bother you, try to overlook so you can enjoy this lovely book. So for those of you 16+ and not impressionable in the least, please read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7674744903835831779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1072406064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1072406064" />
    <a title="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird"><img alt="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343948552p2/10982678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1072406064?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire (Book Blog Bird)" href="/user/show/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird">Claire (Book Blog Bird)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17913785-the-universe-versus-alex-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10982678-claire-book-blog-bird?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1072406064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12372843635697987420">This review is also on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookblogbird.weebly.com'>www.bookblogbird.weebly.com</a><br/><br/>When a book opens with a seventeen year old protagonist beings stopped at Dover customs in the middle of what seems to be a nervous breakdown, with a large bag of marijuana and an urn full of ashes on the passenger seat, you know there’s going to be some pretty interesting explanations coming up.<br/><br/>The Universe vs Alex Woods tells the story of Alex who, as a ten year old, was hit on the head by a tiny meteorite. This fantastically improbabl</span>
  <span id="freeText12372843635697987420" style="display:none">This review is also on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookblogbird.weebly.com">www.bookblogbird.weebly.com</a><br /><br />When a book opens with a seventeen year old protagonist beings stopped at Dover customs in the middle of what seems to be a nervous breakdown, with a large bag of marijuana and an urn full of ashes on the passenger seat, you know there’s going to be some pretty interesting explanations coming up.<br /><br />The Universe vs Alex Woods tells the story of Alex who, as a ten year old, was hit on the head by a tiny meteorite. This fantastically improbable accident lead to Alex developing epilepsy, missing a whole chunk of school and becoming kind of an oddball. Whilst running away from the school bullies one day, Alex meets Mr Peterson, a curmudgeonly Vietnam veteran. They bond over a mutual love of Kurt Vonnegut and become unlikely friends.<br /><br />I absolutely fell for this book and it’s become one that I keep recommending to people, to the point where they say, ‘Yeah, it’s okay. You already told us how much you loved that book.’<br /><br />Alex’s voice is very hard to sum up. His epilepsy caused him to miss a large portion of secondary school and as a result he is very awkward socially, a misfit, pretty geeky (and not in a good way). He doesn’t really get euphemisms or sarcasm and seems a little naive for his years, but despite this (or maybe because of it) at times he just seems to cut through to the truth of things. The chapter where Alex explains misuse of the word ‘gay’ is hands-down the funniest thing I read all year.<br /><br />I really liked Alex’s mum - it was really refreshing to read about a single parent and someone who lives a very alternative lifestyle (she is a clairvoyant and owns a tarot card shop) who isn’t a flake or dropout. Mr Peterson was superb, as was Alex’s friendship with Ellie, the foul-mouthed girl in the year above. <br /><br />The storyline itself has many strands. It’s about the difficulty of social acceptance, coming of age, friendships, the right to die, all of which are dealt with sensitively and thought-provokingly, but also with humour and the ending was one of the most moving I’ve ever read.<br /><br />10/10<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12372843635697987420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_694535294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694535294" />
    <a title="Jacki (Julia Flyte)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2095931-jacki-julia-flyte"><img alt="Jacki (Julia Flyte)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494360994p2/2095931.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694535294?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacki (Julia Flyte)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacki (Julia Flyte)" href="/user/show/2095931-jacki-julia-flyte">Jacki (Julia Flyte)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694535294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12250908534010167220">I fell heavily for this book. In turn funny, heartwarming, clever and tearjerking, it's an absolute delight from its immediately engaging start through to its finish. It's about (and narrated by) Alex Woods, a quirky, bookish, misfit teen who has suffered from epilepsy since he was hit by a meteor at the age of 10. He befriends an older man, Mr Peterson, and among other things, they bond over a love of Kurt Vonnegut novels. We know from the opening paragraph that Mr Peterson will die, but the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText12250908534010167220" style="display:none">I fell heavily for this book. In turn funny, heartwarming, clever and tearjerking, it's an absolute delight from its immediately engaging start through to its finish. It's about (and narrated by) Alex Woods, a quirky, bookish, misfit teen who has suffered from epilepsy since he was hit by a meteor at the age of 10. He befriends an older man, Mr Peterson, and among other things, they bond over a love of Kurt Vonnegut novels. We know from the opening paragraph that Mr Peterson will die, but the book takes a long time to work its way back to the story behind how that happens - and why Alex becomes the subject of a police hunt. <br /><br />Why this book works so well is not in what happens (which is only borderline believable), but the delightful way that Alex tells us his story and gets us to care so much about his fate. The book succeeds in tackling some heavy subjects but in a way that isn't remotely hard going. Alex's deadpan humour and unusual take on events is simply delightful to read. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12250908534010167220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_633327493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633327493" />
    <a title="Ceecee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10394610-ceecee"><img alt="Ceecee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456943309p2/10394610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633327493?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceecee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceecee" href="/user/show/10394610-ceecee">Ceecee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316246606" href="/book/show/15984506-the-universe-versus-alex-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=great-endings">great-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=needs-a-reread">needs-a-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=need-to-own">need-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10394610-ceecee?shelf=netgalley-arc">netgalley-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633327493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16522051021611864455"><b>Well, here's the thing, if a book has:</b><br/><br/>*An introverted bookworm epileptic who loves learning about math, physics, astronomy, and who openly admits that his hobbies are definitely "gay" (in the high school context)<br/>*Unexpected friendships<br/>*Classical music<br/>*Book discussions<br/>*A dog<br/>*Questions about Life and Death and the Universe<br/><br/>I am bound to want to pick it up. Especially with that kind of synopsis. It's one of those few synopses that are spot on. I am all about curious incidents and unexpected connecti</span>
  <span id="freeText16522051021611864455" style="display:none"><b>Well, here's the thing, if a book has:</b><br /><br />*An introverted bookworm epileptic who loves learning about math, physics, astronomy, and who openly admits that his hobbies are definitely "gay" (in the high school context)<br />*Unexpected friendships<br />*Classical music<br />*Book discussions<br />*A dog<br />*Questions about Life and Death and the Universe<br /><br />I am bound to want to pick it up. Especially with that kind of synopsis. It's one of those few synopses that are spot on. I am all about curious incidents and unexpected connections that form our world. <br /><br /><b>Also, if it has:</b><br /><br />*A hero who writes to the wrongly imprisoned<br />*Terminal illness<br />*A furry animal friend dying <br /><br />Well, of course, it's going to appeal to my sensitivities. It's bound to tug at anyone's heartstrings.<br /><br /><b><i>The Universe Versus Alex Woods</i> is the kind of book that makes you think, compels you to reevaluate your beliefs and the lengths you're willing to take for a friend. </b><br /><br />It starts off at the end, with 17-year old Alex held up at customs because he has 113 lbs of marijuana, and, oh, an urn containing the ashes of one Mr Peterson. How did that happen? Alex takes you back to 7 years ago, when he was struck by a meteor, and then we are treated to Alex Woods Growing Up.<br /><br />I can't say this is a coming-of-age story, though, because Alex is pretty much mature for his age already. <b>Instead, this is a story about how little incidents in our lives influence events in the future.</b> You will have to ask yourself, if these series of incidents didn't happen to Alex, would his life have been different? If I had chosen to take the bus instead of walking, would I be with my boyfriend right now? And similar questions, which <b>makes life so damn confusing and yet amazing</b>. In a way, this book is a celebration of that.<br /><br />I suppose people could easily compare this with Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time, and all those other books with introverted young men who are fascinated with math and sciences. Alex is introverted, but is it because he was struck by a meteor, became epileptic, held behind a grade, that he was isolated from his peers? Was Alex autistic? Personally, I don't think so. In any case, I found I liked Alex because he was such a nerd and didn't compromise his principles (such a precocious kid!) to be accepted. I also liked that he was thoughtful and yet sensitive. <br /><br />The other characters (except for the bullies) are also easy to care about. I also liked that it incorporated Kurt Vonnegut and how fitting his novels are to Alex and Mr Peterson's lives. <b>And of course, the classical music</b>. If a book makes you want to learn more about stuff, and makes you want to go read all of Kurt Vonnegut's books, then it can't be all bad.<br /><br />Reading Alex Woods was enjoyable and thought-provoking (there's one major moral dilemma delved into here). And I love books that make me think. It makes that book stay with you for a while longer. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The ultimate moral dilemma here, of course, is do we really have the right to our death? Assisted Suicide was new to me, but I found that it was not appalling at all. This part of the story was handled really well by the author. As a nurse, I've seen too many patients who suffered unnecessarily, sometimes because the family decides for them, or the elderly were too weak to decide for themselves. The only thing to do for them is to give them a dignified death. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Since this was my first NetGalley ARC, I didn't know it had an expiration date, so I chose one of the ARCs I received and read it. I found I did not want to put it down.<br /><br />The only thing I can really criticize about it is that sometimes Alex would be narrating too much, like detailed descriptions of what seizures are, the asteroid belt, etc. I found the dialogues are much more strongly written, and a more effective way of propelling the story forward, rather than plainly Alex telling us what he thought or learned. Aside from that, I really liked the book.<br /><br /><br /><b>*4.5 stars</b> A book that lingers, and made me want to start at the beginning again. A well-written debut book and a worthy read.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.netgalley.com/catalog/show?id=24935" rel="nofollow noopener">~The ebook was provided to me through NetGalley~</a><br />I believe it's still available until July 30.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16522051021611864455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_752669204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752669204" />
    <a title="N.E. David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15944103-n-e-david"><img alt="N.E. David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442656213p2/15944103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/752669204?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="N.E. David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="N.E. David" href="/user/show/15944103-n-e-david">N.E. David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752669204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10040165328911705512">I first met Gavin Extence at a booklaunch in Waterstones in York. He attracted quite a following and I naturally wondered why. I met him again a few months later at Wakefield Literary Festival. Another following. This time I discovered that he is not only a remarkably nice young man but that he has also written a remarkably good book. No wonder he's popular.<br/>His followers are predominantly women. That's no surprise in literary circles as the vast majority of readers are female, a fact prospective</span>
  <span id="freeText10040165328911705512" style="display:none">I first met Gavin Extence at a booklaunch in Waterstones in York. He attracted quite a following and I naturally wondered why. I met him again a few months later at Wakefield Literary Festival. Another following. This time I discovered that he is not only a remarkably nice young man but that he has also written a remarkably good book. No wonder he's popular.<br />His followers are predominantly women. That's no surprise in literary circles as the vast majority of readers are female, a fact prospective authors would do well to recognise. You will guess from this that his book is neither an SAS thriller nor an historical naval drama but it's rather about character and relationships - two compelling characters (Alex Woods and Mr Peterson) and a binding relationship. It's also about assisted suicide and so it has a strong and contemporary theme. These three things alone (character, relationships and theme) are likely to make it a good book but then there's the writing - and that's good too. Mr Extence's prose flows easily across the page but is never in danger of becoming poetic or flowery. A good story, well told - what more could you want?<br />I've heard it said that if you enjoyed The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time you will also enjoy The Universe Versus Alex Woods. And so you might, but not for the obvious reason. True, Alex is a 'challenged' teenager ('gay' as he chooses to describe himself - but not in the sexual sense) as is Christopher Boone in The Curious Incident, but Alex's disability (epilepsy) is not central to the book as is Christopher's autism. Alex will always be an outsider at school, epilepsy or not. What makes both these books enjoyable are those three essential ingredients of character, plot and theme - ie. the basics.<br />If I were to pick a couple of nits with The Universe it would be these. Firstly, the word 'blocky' which I had never heard before but which Mr Extence used repeatedly until it got on my nerves. But far more importantly, his need to 'book-end' the story by starting with Alex's arrival at Dover Customs. This admittedly makes for an interesting and engaging beginning - what is he doing there? where has he come from? and why has he got a stash of marijuana and several hundred pounds in cash? We would naturally like to know. But in terms of timeline, this part of the story belongs to the ending - what is it doing here? The answer, I suspect, is the modern requirement to provide an opening that is designed to ensnare the reader. I shouldn't complain, I did it myself in BIRDS OF THE NILE, but who was I trying to please? Myself, my agent, my publisher or the reader? One wonders ...<br />But none of these things detract from what is an extremely good book. I know Mr Extence is hard at work on another. The test of his ability as a writer will be if he can produce something equally as compelling but in a different voice. If he can, I will certainly be interested in reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10040165328911705512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3941502-peggy?shelf=really-awesome-books">really-awesome-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer802317556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14898297522669831434">It's always great when you read a book that you have been wanting to read for a long time, that you have high expectations for, that has been rated highly by your GR friends, to actually be a 5 star read. It's even greater to read a book that you have no expectations of, hardly heard about before you started reading it, and has no indication of greatness based on your friends ratings because no one has read it, and to find out that that book is worth 5 stars. <br/><br/>What a wonderful story. Alex is one </span>
  <span id="freeText14898297522669831434" style="display:none">It's always great when you read a book that you have been wanting to read for a long time, that you have high expectations for, that has been rated highly by your GR friends, to actually be a 5 star read. It's even greater to read a book that you have no expectations of, hardly heard about before you started reading it, and has no indication of greatness based on your friends ratings because no one has read it, and to find out that that book is worth 5 stars. <br /><br />What a wonderful story. Alex is one of my favourite book characters of this year, I just loved the way he talks and thinks and tells us about the past 7 years of his life. I wish there were lots more Alex's in the world, it would make the world such a better place. The story itself is sweet and heartwarming. It's also funny and sad, not in the laugh-out-loud or cry-out-loud way, but in that same sweet and heartwarming and beautiful way that all of the book makes you feel. I'm sitting here, having finished the book, and I'm feeling content and pleased and satisfied and have a smile on my face and feel like all is right in the world, and for me, that's the best way to feel after finishing a book. </span>

<div id="review_527303513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527303513" />
    <a title="Marleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/348805-marleen"><img alt="Marleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1225138538p2/348805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527303513?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marleen" href="/user/show/348805-marleen">Marleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444765885" href="/book/show/16082950-the-universe-versus-alex-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527303513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16056241205792945704">I received this book from Hodder & Stoughton through Nudge.<br/><br/>“Full explanations are much messier. They can’t be conveyed in five unprepared stop-start minutes. You have to give them time and space to unfold. (…) I’m going to tell you my story, the full story, in the manner I think it should be told.”<br/><br/>Alex Wood is not your average teenager. He didn’t have a conventional start to his life. With a clairvoyant mother who doesn’t know who his father is his life was always going to be a little bit differ</span>
  <span id="freeText16056241205792945704" style="display:none">I received this book from Hodder &amp; Stoughton through Nudge.<br /><br />“Full explanations are much messier. They can’t be conveyed in five unprepared stop-start minutes. You have to give them time and space to unfold. (…) I’m going to tell you my story, the full story, in the manner I think it should be told.”<br /><br />Alex Wood is not your average teenager. He didn’t have a conventional start to his life. With a clairvoyant mother who doesn’t know who his father is his life was always going to be a little bit different. Things really change though when Alex is ten years old and gets hit on the head by a meteorite. When he wakes up after two weeks in a coma his life has changed. He discovers that he has become something of a celebrity, that his hair will not grow back over his scar and that he will have to contend with epileptic fits from now on. After a year of forced house-arrest to come to terms with his fits and the medication he takes for it, Alex has a hard time fitting back into school and life in general. <br /><br />When an unfortunate incident involving three bullies, a greenhouse and an epileptic fit bring Alex into contact with Mr. Peterson, it is the start of a remarkable and very special friendship. <br /><br />“The first thing I learnt that day was this: what you think you know about a person is only a fraction of the story.”<br /><br />The young boy and the older man grow close through a shared love for classical music and Kurt Vonnegut novels. When Mr. Peterson is diagnosed with a debilitating and fatal disease which will force him to face a slow and excruciating death his options are limited. With Alex’ help and determination though, Mr. Peterson finds that he is able to make the decisions he wants to make. And Alex has no regrets. Not even when, aged 17, he is apprehended in Dover with an urn of ashes on the passenger seat of his car and a bag of marijuana in the glove compartment. The whole of England may be in an uproar about his recent journey; Alex knows he’s done the right thing.<br /><br />This is a very special book. At first glance it is a charming coming of age story about a young man with a less than conventional life. On further inspection though this proves to be a thought-provoking work of fiction dealing with weighty subjects such as bullying, illness, life, death, euthanasia and personal responsibility. <br />“Understanding and accepting that you have a permanent illness does not mean being a slave to it. It’s the first step you have to make so that you can go on living your life.”<br /><br />And yet this book doesn’t read like a work that is trying to convey a message. This book doesn’t preach, doesn’t try to convince the reader about anything and is remarkably – even deceptively – easy to read. And yet it poses an important question: should we, or should we not have the right to decide when to end our own lives? I realise that this makes the book sound as if it will be a depressing and heavy read, but it isn’t. The sad and reflective sections in this book are perfectly balanced by the lighter and at times laugh out loud funny parts. The differences between young, curious and innocent Alex and the older and world-weary Mr. Peterson are at times very funny; a delight of confusion and misunderstandings. At the same time their friendship is wonderful; these two characters enrich each other’s lives in a multitude of ways. <br /><br />Gavin Extence hits the voice of young Alex spot-on. He brings this character who is older than his years in some ways, yet very innocent in others, to life in a way that made me want to go and find him. The writing in this book is smooth and takes the reader on an emotionally charged journey they won’t want to end. <br /><br />This is also a wonderful book for those who love reading. We meet Kurt Vonnegut’s books in rather poignant ways and are also treated to parts of Catch 22 with equal relevance to the story in this book.<br /><br />Beautiful, funny, heartbreaking, thought-provoking, very clever and original this is the best book I’ve read so far this year and will, undoubtedly, end up among my favourites for 2013. I can’t rave enough about this book; it is nothing short of brilliant.<br /><br />I’ll give the final word to Mr. Peterson:<br /><br />“In the long history of human affairs, common sense doesn’t have the greatest track record.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16056241205792945704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_659079684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659079684" />
    <a title="L.A." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4055856-l-a"><img alt="L.A." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359411127p2/4055856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659079684?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L.A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="L.A." href="/user/show/4055856-l-a">L.A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4055856-l-a?shelf=imagination">imagination</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4055856-l-a?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4055856-l-a?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4055856-l-a?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4055856-l-a?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659079684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7726200416209832707">Posted first on Blog critics<br/><br/>Every now and then a book comes along that takes you in directions that are unexpected. When differing backgrounds collide we are often surprised at the outcome. Such is the experience of reading The Universe Versus Alex Woods by Gavin Extence.<br/><br/>Alex Woods lives in an oddly disjointed world. His mother is a bit different than other mothers, and he doesn’t know his dad. He also has the distinction of having been struck by a meteor when he was 10 years old. This added to </span>
  <span id="freeText7726200416209832707" style="display:none">Posted first on Blog critics<br /><br />Every now and then a book comes along that takes you in directions that are unexpected. When differing backgrounds collide we are often surprised at the outcome. Such is the experience of reading The Universe Versus Alex Woods by Gavin Extence.<br /><br />Alex Woods lives in an oddly disjointed world. His mother is a bit different than other mothers, and he doesn’t know his dad. He also has the distinction of having been struck by a meteor when he was 10 years old. This added to his woes growing up, leaving scars that are hard to ignore. Being very intelligent and rather bookish, he draws the ire of bullies at school.<br /><br />Escaping these bullies is what brings an elderly reclusive widower, Mr. Peterson, into his life. In an effort to hide from those making his life miserable, Alex stumbles upon his garden and hothouse, where he finds safety hiding in a shed. Unwilling to let him go, those who are trying to make his life miserable vandalize the property.<br />When Mr. Peterson investigates the noise, he finds only Alex in the shambles of his garden. Alex knows from experience he can’t rat on those responsible, as his life will only get worse, yet he tries to convince Mr. Peterson of his innocence.<br /><br />Even his mother is not a believer, so she overrides the objections from both sides and as punishment makes Alex report every day after school to help Mr. Peterson out. Little to either of them realize, they have a great deal to learn from each other. Due to the nature of Alex’s injury, he is a well-known personality, recognized everywhere he goes. Whether this is a hindrance or a help, he is not sure, but it certainly makes allowances for the strange existence he leads.<br />Mr. Peterson has his own problems, and since the death of his wife he wants nothing to do with the outside world. As his world collides with that of Alex, neither of them realizes the impact that such a fateful meeting will create.<br /><br />The Universe Versus Alex Woods could be considered a young adult novel, yet there is a depth of meaning and perception that make it one step more. The morals and events that are threaded throughout are at times funny, yet also tragic. The story draws you in, dragging you along step by step as Alex and Mr. Peterson take on the very fundamentals of human rights, as well as the tragedy of everyday living.<br /><br />If you enjoy interesting and unique experiences, you will find this to be the must-read of the summer. Not my usual reading material, I was at once charmed and enthralled. Beginning with Alex and how he developed his own personality, and moving toward a tragic and yet uplifting ending you will be hard pressed to put this work down.<br /><br />The Universe Versus Alex Woods would be a great book for either a reading group or discussion group. It’s a must-have for your library, and a treat for both the young, as well as the young at heart. There is some very deep subject matter discussed, yet the end result is extraordinary. Gavin Extence is an author to watch for.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7726200416209832707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_749431030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/749431030" />
    <a title="Robert Blumenthal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10110896-robert-blumenthal"><img alt="Robert Blumenthal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339293952p2/10110896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/749431030?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Blumenthal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Blumenthal" href="/user/show/10110896-robert-blumenthal">Robert Blumenthal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer749431030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7044946149627283150">For most of its 400 plus pages, this is a simply wonderful novel. My only complaint is that it was just a tad too long. I would have edited about 25-50 pages from it. That being said, I found the young narrator to be a totally wonderful character, and this rates as an excellent British coming-of-age novel. At the age of ten, Alex is struck in the head by a meteorite and miraculously survives with no more disability than epilepsy (not to downplay the significant disability that epilepsy is, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText7044946149627283150" style="display:none">For most of its 400 plus pages, this is a simply wonderful novel. My only complaint is that it was just a tad too long. I would have edited about 25-50 pages from it. That being said, I found the young narrator to be a totally wonderful character, and this rates as an excellent British coming-of-age novel. At the age of ten, Alex is struck in the head by a meteorite and miraculously survives with no more disability than epilepsy (not to downplay the significant disability that epilepsy is, but the damage could have been so much more extreme brain damage). After various school experiences (most of them negative), he meets Isaac Peterson, a curmudgeon older American Vietnam veteran who becomes a mentor for Alex. Their relationship is deftly developed, and there is much humor and interesting plot developments. In the end, a huge and difficult task is asked of Alex and his decision whether or not to do it will have a profound effect on his life. I found that I flew through this book--it is very readable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7044946149627283150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1320162262" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1320162262" />
    <a title="Mich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36926403-mich"><img alt="Mich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597760595p2/36926403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1320162262?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mich" href="/user/show/36926403-mich">Mich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444765892" href="/book/show/17904603-the-universe-versus-alex-woods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36926403-mich?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36926403-mich?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1320162262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12376760581338331438"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>*Trigger warnings: epilepsy, bullying, suicide, terminal illness, substance use.<br/>**Also mind the use of some words that are considered slurs (read from a book or mentioned in conversations).<br/>***Long review.</i><br/><br/><br/>I guess it's wisest to start with a little piece of information of the titular role himself. <i>"Born to clairvoyance mother and phantom father, Alex Woods didn't have the most conventional start in life"</i>. As if it wasn't enough, an improbable event hit him (literally) when he was ten; in </span>
  <span id="freeText12376760581338331438" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>*Trigger warnings: epilepsy, bullying, suicide, terminal illness, substance use.<br />**Also mind the use of some words that are considered slurs (read from a book or mentioned in conversations).<br />***Long review.</i><br /><br /><br />I guess it's wisest to start with a little piece of information of the titular role himself. <i>"Born to clairvoyance mother and phantom father, Alex Woods didn't have the most conventional start in life"</i>. As if it wasn't enough, an improbable event hit him (literally) when he was ten; in a broad daylight, in his own kitchen. Of all the places in the world, of all the wide landscape surrounding his suburban house, of all the space in his kitchen, a meteor chose to land on his head, making him a sensation in the country, making him <i>the</i> Alex Woods.<br /><br />The book began much, much later in his life, on the day he was stopped at the Dover customs when he re-entered the UK. He was seventeen, disoriented, in somebody else's car, with 113 grams of marijuana in its compartment, and an urn filled with someone's remaining, sending the country in an uproar for the second time in his life. How he ended up in that position that day was still in question, and in the next chapters, in the remaining 391 pages, Alex would take you all the way back from the beginning: the day that alien stone fell upon him seven years ago.<br /><br />Unfortunately, getting hit in the head by 4 kilograms of something out of this world (literally) didn't put Alex in anything close to extraordinary life, instead it put him in the hospital, not just once, not just twice, but a few times a year. Being epileptic made him prone to bullies, and given what I told you about his parents, you know the deal. He was having hard time growing up, especially when your ride-or-die is a grumpy old Vietnam veteran.<br /><br />This book mostly focused on (but not limited to) the friendship between Alex and Mr Peterson. Having no father figure before, Alex quickly bonded with the old Mr Peterson after their unlikely meeting in one afternoon. During the span of their friendship were discussions about life and death, beliefs, classical music, war, Kurt Vonnegut, and many more. Also along with the discussions and arguments they had had, was how oddly lifechanging they were to each other.<br /><br />Alex's character was incredible. It wasn't the epitome of a perfect character development, but with a character as complex as Alex, Gavin Extence did a hell of a terrific research. Some characters were unlikeable for me, but in a broader view, I valued how Alex behave towards any of them, and no matter how he was treated and no matter what his reaction was, I'd always think "that sounds like a very Alex thing Alex would do/say". Also the things he said often cracked me up.<br /><br />This book is also full of narratives about science, medicine, and astronomy, but for some reasons they weren't hard at all to understand. It was surprisingly an easy read for me. Somehow this book gave me the 60s sci-fi/retro aesthetic feels, especially when Alex and Mr Peterson were geeking about Kurt Vonnegut's books together, and it made me want to read his works.<br /><br />I'm quite surprised that this book isn't as "popular" as the others in the bookish world. There are many things to discuss. I'm glad I decided to buy it off an online book bazaar in the last minutes. It was like 70% off and I didn't even realize that it had been on my reading list from like 2015. I guess it was a part of the strange series of events that brought Alex Woods to me. What a read, heartwarming and heartbreaking at the same time, and that's <i>something</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12376760581338331438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
